</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Intercity-Express</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Ice Train" redirects here. For professional wrestler, see <a href="/wiki/Ice_Train_(wrestler)" title="Ice Train (wrestler)">Ice Train (wrestler)</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Intercity-Express (disambiguation)">Intercity-Express (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<td><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bahn.com/en/view/trains/long-distance/ice-ice-sprinter.shtml">www<wbr />.bahn<wbr />.com<wbr />/en<wbr />/view<wbr />/trains<wbr />/long-distance<wbr />/ice-ice-sprinter<wbr />.shtml</a></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>Intercity-Express</b> (written as <b>InterCityExpress</b> in <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> and, formerly, in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>) or <b>ICE</b> (<small>German pronunciation:</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[iːtseːˈʔeː]</a></span>) is a system of <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed trains</a> <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Germany" title="High-speed rail in Germany">predominantly running in Germany</a> and its surrounding countries. It is the highest service category offered by <a href="/wiki/DB_Fernverkehr" title="DB Fernverkehr">DB Fernverkehr</a> and is the flagship of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a>. The brand name "ICE" is among the best-known in Germany, with a brand awareness close to 100%, according to DB.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> There are currently 259 trainsets in five different versions of the ICE vehicles in use, named <a href="/wiki/ICE_1" title="ICE 1">ICE 1</a> (deployed in 1991), <a href="/wiki/ICE_2" title="ICE 2">ICE 2</a> (1996), <a href="/wiki/ICE_T" title="ICE T">ICE T</a> (1999), <a href="/wiki/ICE_3" title="ICE 3">ICE 3</a> (1999) and <a href="/wiki/ICE_TD" title="ICE TD">ICE TD</a> (2001–2003, back in service 2007). The ICE 3, including its variant models, is made by a consortium led by <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>.</p>
<p>Procurement of a further version, <a href="/wiki/ICx" class="mw-redirect" title="ICx">ICx</a>, began c. 2008, and was rebranded <a href="/wiki/ICE_4" class="mw-redirect" title="ICE 4">ICE 4</a> in late 2015. Introduction of the trains are expected from 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.</p>
<p>Apart from domestic use, the trains can also be seen in countries neighbouring Germany. There are, for example, ICE&#160;1 lines to <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zurich" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich">Zurich</a>. ICE&#160;3 trains also run to <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Liège (city)">Liège</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> and at lower speeds to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> On 10 June 2007, <a href="/wiki/LGV_Est" title="LGV Est">a new line between Paris and Frankfurt/Stuttgart</a> was opened, jointly operated by ICE and <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a> trains. ICE trains to London via the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a> were planned for 2018, however DB has stated it is awaiting new class 407 rolling stock before it can run the route. DB received its certificate to run trains through the tunnel in June 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-bahn.com_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bahn.com-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-london_delay_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-london_delay-5">[5]</a></sup> While ICE&#160;3M trains operate the Paris-Frankfurt service (with the exception of trains 9553/9552, which operate with <a href="/wiki/SNCF_TGV_Duplex" title="SNCF TGV Duplex">TGV Duplex</a> equipment and are cross-crewed with both SNCF and DB staff), SNCF's <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a> runs from Paris to Munich (via Stuttgart), with mixed crews on both trains.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> German and Austrian ICE&#160;T trains run to <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>. On 9 December 2007, the ICE TD was introduced on the service from Berlin via <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> to the Danish cities of <a href="/wiki/Aarhus" title="Aarhus">Aarhus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>.</p>
<p>The Spanish railway operator <a href="/wiki/RENFE" class="mw-redirect" title="RENFE">RENFE</a> also employs trains based on the ICE 3 (<a href="/wiki/Siemens_Velaro" title="Siemens Velaro">Siemens Velaro</a>) called <a href="/wiki/AVE_Class_103" title="AVE Class 103">AVE Class 103</a> which are certified to run at speeds up to 350&#160;km/h.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Wider versions were ordered by China for the <a href="/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Tianjin_Intercity_Railway" title="Beijing–Tianjin Intercity Railway">Beijing–Tianjin Intercity Railway</a> link (<a href="/wiki/Siemens_Velaro#Velaro_CRH3" title="Siemens Velaro">CRH 3</a>) and by Russia for the Moscow – <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> and Moscow – <a href="/wiki/Nizhny_Novgorod" title="Nizhny Novgorod">Nizhny Novgorod</a> routes (<a href="/wiki/Siemens_Velaro#Velaro_RUS" title="Siemens Velaro">Velaro RUS</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/InterCityExperimental" title="InterCityExperimental">InterCityExperimental</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

</td>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:410001MKF_Zug_1152.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/410001MKF_Zug_1152.jpg/220px-410001MKF_Zug_1152.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/410001MKF_Zug_1152.jpg/330px-410001MKF_Zug_1152.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/410001MKF_Zug_1152.jpg/440px-410001MKF_Zug_1152.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1152" data-file-height="768" /></a>

InterCityExperimental (ICE V) first run as a full train, near Munich (Sept. 1985)</div>
</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bundesbahn" title="Deutsche Bundesbahn">Deutsche Bundesbahn</a> started a series of trials in 1985 using the <a href="/wiki/InterCityExperimental" title="InterCityExperimental">InterCityExperimental</a> (also called ICE-V) test train. The IC Experimental was used as a showcase train and for high-speed trials, setting a new <a href="/wiki/Land_speed_record_for_railed_vehicles" class="mw-redirect" title="Land speed record for railed vehicles">world speed record</a> at 406.9&#160;km/h (253&#160;mph) on 1 May 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-transrapid-buch_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transrapid-buch-10">[10]</a></sup> The train was retired in 1996 and replaced with a new trial unit, called the <a href="/wiki/ICE-S" class="mw-redirect" title="ICE-S">ICE S</a>.</p>
<p>After extensive discussion between the Bundesbahn and the Ministry of Transport regarding onboard equipment, length and width of the train and the number of trainsets required, a first batch of 41 units was ordered in 1988. The order was extended to 60 units in 1990, with <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> in mind. However, not all trains could be delivered in time.</p>
<p>The ICE network was officially inaugurated on 29 May 1991 with several vehicles converging on the newly built station <a href="/wiki/Kassel-Wilhelmsh%C3%B6he_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe railway station">Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe</a> from different directions.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_generation">First generation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: First generation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE1_Schellenberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/ICE1_Schellenberg.jpg/220px-ICE1_Schellenberg.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/ICE1_Schellenberg.jpg/330px-ICE1_Schellenberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/ICE1_Schellenberg.jpg/440px-ICE1_Schellenberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE1_Schellenberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ICE 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg-Munich_high-speed_rail_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuremberg-Munich high-speed rail line">Nuremberg-Ingolstadt line</a> (Dec. 2006)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ICE_1" title="ICE 1">ICE 1</a></div>
<p>The first ICE trains were the trainsets of <a href="/wiki/ICE_1" title="ICE 1">ICE 1</a> (power cars: Class&#160;401), which came into service in 1989. The first regularly scheduled ICE trains ran from 2 June 1991 from <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Altona_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg-Altona railway station">Hamburg-Altona</a> via <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Hauptbahnhof" title="Hamburg Hauptbahnhof">Hamburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Hannover_Hauptbahnhof" title="Hannover Hauptbahnhof">Hannover Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Kassel-Wilhelmsh%C3%B6he_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe railway station">Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe</a> – <a href="/wiki/Fulda_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulda railway station">Fulda</a> – <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Main)_Hauptbahnhof" title="Frankfurt (Main) Hauptbahnhof">Frankfurt Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Hauptbahnhof" title="Mannheim Hauptbahnhof">Mannheim Hbf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hauptbahnhof" title="Stuttgart Hauptbahnhof">Stuttgart Hbf</a> toward <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hauptbahnhof" title="München Hauptbahnhof">München Hbf</a> at hourly intervals<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> on the new <b>ICE line 6</b>. The <a href="/wiki/Hanover-W%C3%BCrzburg_high-speed_rail_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanover-Würzburg high-speed rail line">Hanover-Würzburg line</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mannheim-Stuttgart_high-speed_rail_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Mannheim-Stuttgart high-speed rail line">Mannheim-Stuttgart line</a>, which had both opened the same year, were hence integrated into the ICE network from the very beginning.</p>
<p>Due to the lack of trainsets in 1991 and early 1992, the <b>ICE line 4</b> (<a href="/wiki/Bremen_Hauptbahnhof" title="Bremen Hauptbahnhof">Bremen Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Hannover_Hauptbahnhof" title="Hannover Hauptbahnhof">Hannover Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Kassel-Wilhelmsh%C3%B6he_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe railway station">Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe</a> – <a href="/wiki/Fulda_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulda railway station">Fulda</a> – <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg_Hauptbahnhof" title="Würzburg Hauptbahnhof">Würzburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrnberg_Hauptbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Nürnberg Hauptbahnhof">Nürnberg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hauptbahnhof" title="München Hauptbahnhof">München Hbf</a>) couldn't start operating until 1 June 1992. Prior to that date, ICE trainsets were used when available and were integrated in the <a href="/wiki/Intercity_(Deutsche_Bahn)" title="Intercity (Deutsche Bahn)">Intercity</a> network and with IC tariffs.</p>
<p>In 1993, the <b>ICE line 6</b>'s terminus was moved from Hamburg to Berlin (later, in 1998, via the <a href="/wiki/Hanover-Berlin_high-speed_rail_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanover-Berlin high-speed rail line">Hanover-Berlin line</a> and the former <b>IC line 3</b> from <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Altona_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg-Altona railway station">Hamburg-Altona</a> via <a href="/wiki/Hannover_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hannover Hbf">Hannover Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Kassel-Wilhelmsh%C3%B6he_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe railway station">Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe</a> – <a href="/wiki/Fulda_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulda railway station">Fulda</a> – <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Hbf">Frankfurt Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Mannheim Hbf">Mannheim Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Karlsruhe Hbf">Karlsruhe Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Freiburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Freiburg Hbf">Freiburg Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Basel_SBB" class="mw-redirect" title="Basel SBB">Basel SBB</a> was upgraded to ICE standards as a replacement).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_generation">Second generation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Second generation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ICE_2" title="ICE 2">ICE 2</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE2_Hilpodrom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/ICE2_Hilpodrom.jpg/220px-ICE2_Hilpodrom.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/ICE2_Hilpodrom.jpg/330px-ICE2_Hilpodrom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/ICE2_Hilpodrom.jpg/440px-ICE2_Hilpodrom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE2_Hilpodrom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ICE&#160;2 near Ingolstadt (Feb. 2007)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1997, the successor, the <b>ICE&#160;2</b> trains pulled by Class 402 powerheads, was put into service. One of the goals of the ICE&#160;2 was to improve <a href="/wiki/Weight_distribution" title="Weight distribution">load balancing</a> by building smaller train units which could be coupled or detached as needed.</p>
<p>These trainsets were used on the <b>ICE line 10</b> Berlin-Cologne/Bonn. However, since the <a href="/wiki/Control_car_(rail)" class="mw-redirect" title="Control car (rail)">driving van trailers</a> of the trains were still awaiting approval, the DB joined two portions (with one powerhead each) to form a long train, similar to the ICE&#160;1. Only from 24 May 1998 were the ICE 2 units fully equipped with driving van trailers and could be portioned on their run from <a href="/wiki/Hamm_(Westfalen)_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamm (Westfalen) railway station">Hamm</a> via either <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Dortmund Hbf">Dortmund Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Essen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Essen Hbf">Essen Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Duisburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Duisburg Hbf">Duisburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf Hbf">Düsseldorf Hbf</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hagen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hagen Hbf">Hagen Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Wuppertal_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Wuppertal Hbf">Wuppertal Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Solingen_Hauptbahnhof" title="Solingen Hauptbahnhof">Solingen-Ohligs</a>.</p>
<p>In late 1998, the <a href="/wiki/Hanover-Berlin_high-speed_rail_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanover-Berlin high-speed rail line">Hanover-Berlin high-speed rail line</a> was opened as the third <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed line</a> in Germany, cutting travel time on line 10 (between Berlin and the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr valley">Ruhr valley</a>) by 2½ hours.</p>
<p>The ICE 1 and ICE 2 trains' <a href="/wiki/Loading_gauge" title="Loading gauge">loading gauge</a> exceeds that recommended by the international railway organisation <a href="/wiki/International_Union_of_Railways" title="International Union of Railways">UIC</a>. Even though the trains were originally to be used only domestically, some units are licensed to run in Switzerland and Austria. Some ICE 1 units have been equipped with an additional smaller <a href="/wiki/Pantograph_(rail)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pantograph (rail)">pantograph</a> to be able to run on the different Swiss <a href="/wiki/Overhead_lines" class="mw-redirect" title="Overhead lines">overhead wire</a> geometry. All ICE 1 and ICE 2 trains are single-voltage <a href="/wiki/15_kV_AC_railway_electrification" title="15 kV AC railway electrification">15 kV AC</a>, which restricts their radius of operation largely to the German-speaking countries of Europe. ICE 2 trains can run at a top speed of 174&#160;mph (280&#160;km/h).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_generation">Third generation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Third generation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ICE_3" title="ICE 3">ICE 3</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE3_Euerwangtunnel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/ICE3_Euerwangtunnel.jpg/220px-ICE3_Euerwangtunnel.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/ICE3_Euerwangtunnel.jpg/330px-ICE3_Euerwangtunnel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/ICE3_Euerwangtunnel.jpg/440px-ICE3_Euerwangtunnel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE3_Euerwangtunnel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ICE 3 (Class 403) (Mar. 2007)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SiemensVelaroD-InnoTrans2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/SiemensVelaroD-InnoTrans2010.jpg/220px-SiemensVelaroD-InnoTrans2010.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/SiemensVelaroD-InnoTrans2010.jpg/330px-SiemensVelaroD-InnoTrans2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/SiemensVelaroD-InnoTrans2010.jpg/440px-SiemensVelaroD-InnoTrans2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1446" data-file-height="1047" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SiemensVelaroD-InnoTrans2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Latest ICE 3 version, a <a href="/wiki/Siemens_Velaro" title="Siemens Velaro">Siemens Velaro D</a> at InnoTrans 2010, after handover of first train to DB. These trains have been designated The New ICE 3</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To overcome the restrictions imposed on the ICE 1 and ICE 2, their successor, the ICE 3, was built to a smaller <a href="/wiki/Loading_gauge" title="Loading gauge">loading gauge</a> to permit usability throughout the European <a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" title="Standard gauge">standard gauge</a> network (except the UK non-highspeed network) . Unlike their predecessors, the ICE 3 units are built not as locomotive-pulled trains (albeit aerodynamically optimised), but as <a href="/wiki/Electric_multiple_unit" title="Electric multiple unit">electric multiple units</a> with underfloor motors throughout. This also reduced the load per axle and enabled the ICE&#160;3 to comply with the pertinent <a href="/wiki/International_Union_of_Railways" title="International Union of Railways">UIC</a> standard.</p>
<p>Two different classes were developed: the <a href="/wiki/DBAG_Class_403" class="mw-redirect" title="DBAG Class 403">Class 403</a> (domestic ICE 3) and the <a href="/wiki/DBAG_Class_406" class="mw-redirect" title="DBAG Class 406">Class 406</a> (ICE 3M), the M standing for <i>Mehrsystem</i> (<a href="/wiki/Multi-system_locomotive" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-system locomotive">multi-system</a>). The trains were labelled and marketed as the <a href="/wiki/Siemens_Velaro" title="Siemens Velaro">Velaro</a> by their manufacturer, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>.</p>
<p>Just like the ICE&#160;2, the ICE&#160;3 and the ICE&#160;3M were developed as half-length trains (when compared to an ICE&#160;1) and are able to travel in portions, with individual units running on different lines, then being coupled to travel together. Since the ICE 3 trains are the only ones able to run on the <a href="/wiki/Cologne-Frankfurt_high-speed_rail_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Cologne-Frankfurt high-speed rail line">Köln-Frankfurt high-speed line</a> with its 4.0% incline, they are used predominantly on services that utilise this line.</p>
<p>Deutsche Bahn has ordered another 16 units – worth <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a> 495 million – for international traffic, especially to France.</p>
<p>The newest high-speed line in Germany, the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg-Ingolstadt_high-speed_rail_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuremberg-Ingolstadt high-speed rail line">Nuremberg-Ingolstadt high-speed rail line</a>, which opened in May 2006, is the most recent addition to the ICE network. It is one of only two lines in Germany (the other being the Cologne to Frankfurt line) that are equipped for a line speed of 300&#160;km/h. Since only 3rd generation ICE trains can travel at this speed, the <b>ICE line 41</b>, formerly running from <a href="/wiki/Essen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Essen Hbf">Essen Hbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Duisburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Duisburg Hbf">Duisburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Main)_S%C3%BCdbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt (Main) Südbahnhof">Frankfurt Südbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrnberg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Nürnberg Hbf">Nürnberg Hbf</a>, was extended over the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg-Ingolstadt_high-speed_rail_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuremberg-Ingolstadt high-speed rail line">Nuremberg-Ingolstadt high-speed rail line</a> and today the service run is <a href="/wiki/Oberhausen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Oberhausen Hbf">Oberhausen Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Duisburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Duisburg Hbf">Duisburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Hbf">Frankfurt Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrnberg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Nürnberg Hbf">Nürnberg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Ingolstadt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Ingolstadt Hbf">Ingolstadt Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="München Hbf">München Hbf</a>.</p>
<p>The ICE&#160;3 runs at speeds up to 320&#160;km/h (198&#160;mph) on the <a href="/wiki/LGV_Est" title="LGV Est">LGV Est</a> railway <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a> – <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> in France.+</p>
<p>The latest generation ICE 3, <a href="/wiki/DB_Class_407" class="mw-redirect" title="DB Class 407">Class 407</a>, is known as the New ICE 3, and is part of the Siemens Velaro family with the model designation Velaro D. It currently runs on many services in Germany and through to other countries like France. These trains were meant for the planned Deutsche Bahn services through the channel tunnel to London. Due to delay in the delivery of the new Velaro D rolling stock the London service was cancelled<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fourth_Generation">Fourth Generation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Fourth Generation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ICE_4_(Deutsche_Bahn)" title="ICE 4 (Deutsche Bahn)">ICE 4 (Deutsche Bahn)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_4_Pr%C3%A4sentation_Berlin_Hbf_(039).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/ICE_4_Pr%C3%A4sentation_Berlin_Hbf_%28039%29.jpg/220px-ICE_4_Pr%C3%A4sentation_Berlin_Hbf_%28039%29.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/ICE_4_Pr%C3%A4sentation_Berlin_Hbf_%28039%29.jpg/330px-ICE_4_Pr%C3%A4sentation_Berlin_Hbf_%28039%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/ICE_4_Pr%C3%A4sentation_Berlin_Hbf_%28039%29.jpg/440px-ICE_4_Pr%C3%A4sentation_Berlin_Hbf_%28039%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5312" data-file-height="2988" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_4_Pr%C3%A4sentation_Berlin_Hbf_(039).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ICE 4 presentation at the Berlin Central Station, September 14, 2016.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Procurement of ICx trainsets started c.2008 as replacements for locomotive hauled <a href="/wiki/InterCity" title="InterCity">InterCity</a> and <a href="/wiki/EuroCity" title="EuroCity">EuroCity</a> train services- the scope was later expanded to include replacements for <a href="/wiki/ICE_1" title="ICE 1">ICE 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/ICE_2" title="ICE 2">ICE 2</a> trainsets. In 2011 <a href="/wiki/Siemens_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Siemens AG">Siemens AG</a> was awarded the contract for 130 seven car intercity train replacements, and 90 ten car ICE train replacements, plus further options - the contract for the ten car sets was modified 2013 to expand the trainset length to twelve vehicles. The name <i><b>ICx</b></i> was used for the trains during the initial stages of the procurement; in late 2015 the trains were rebranded <b>ICE 4</b>, at the unveiling of the first trainset, and given the class designation 412 by Deutsche Bahn.</p>
<p>Two pre-production trainsets were manufactured and used for testing prior to introduction of the main series.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ICE_T_and_ICE_TD">ICE T and ICE TD</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: ICE T and ICE TD">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE-TVienna.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/ICE-TVienna.JPG/220px-ICE-TVienna.JPG" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/ICE-TVienna.JPG/330px-ICE-TVienna.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/ICE-TVienna.JPG/440px-ICE-TVienna.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2563" data-file-height="1809" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE-TVienna.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ICE-T (Class 411) tilting train (Mar. 2007)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Simultaneously with the ICE 3, Siemens developed trains with <a href="/wiki/Tilting_train" title="Tilting train">tilting</a> technology, using much of the ICE 3 technical design. The class 411 (seven cars) and 415 (five cars) ICE T EMUs and class 605 ICE TD DMUs (four cars) were built with a similar interior and exterior design. They were specially designed for older railway lines not suitable for high speeds, for example the twisting lines in <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a>. ICE-TD has diesel traction. ICE-T and ICE-TD can be operated jointly, but this is not done routinely.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ICE_T">ICE T</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: ICE T">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ICE_T" title="ICE T">ICE T</a></div>
<p>A total of 60 class 411 and 11 class 415 have been built so far (units built after 2004 belong to the modified second generation ICE-T2 batch). Both classes work reliably. Austria's <a href="/wiki/%C3%96BB" class="mw-redirect" title="ÖBB">ÖBB</a> purchased three units in 2007, operating them jointly with DB. It might be worth noting that even though DB assigned the name <i>ICE-T</i> to class 411/415, the <i>T</i> originally did not stand for <i>tilting</i>, but for <i>Triebwagen</i> (railcar), as DB's marketing department at first deemed the top speed too low for assignment of the InterCityExpress brand and therefore planned to refer to this class as <i>IC-T</i> (InterCity-Triebwagen). The trainsets of the T series were manufactured in 1999. The tilting system has been provided by <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Ferroviaria" title="Fiat Ferroviaria">Fiat Ferroviaria</a>, now part of <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a>. ICE T trains can run at speeds of up to 140&#160;mph (230&#160;km/h).</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ICE_TD">ICE TD</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: ICE TD">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BahnRatekau.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/BahnRatekau.jpg/220px-BahnRatekau.jpg" width="220" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/BahnRatekau.jpg/330px-BahnRatekau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/BahnRatekau.jpg/440px-BahnRatekau.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="515" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BahnRatekau.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ICE TD in service of DB in Northern Germany</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ICE_TD" title="ICE TD">ICE TD</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Siemens_Venturio" title="Siemens Venturio">Siemens Venturio</a></div>
<p>Rather ill-fated was the adoption of diesel services. In 2001, a total of 20 units were commissioned for use on the <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>-<a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>-<a href="/wiki/Zurich" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich">Zurich</a> lines, but these class 605 (ICE-TD) units experienced trouble from the start so the trains were mothballed. During the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>, they were used for supplemental services. Their top speed is 125&#160;mph (200&#160;km/h). They are expensive to use within Germany since full diesel tax must be paid. Starting at the end of 2007, the class 605 has been deployed on the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>-<a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> route. This route, using the <a href="/wiki/Fehmarn_Belt" title="Fehmarn Belt">Fehmarn Belt</a> <a href="/wiki/Train_ferry" title="Train ferry">train ferry</a> needs diesel trains for both the railway and the ferry, as neither has an electric supply. Later the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>-<a href="/wiki/Aarhus" title="Aarhus">Aarhus</a> started to use these trains. The Danish railway currently has a severe shortage of long-distance diesel trains since their new <a href="/wiki/IC4" title="IC4">IC4</a>, with features similar to the ICE-TD, has also been ill-fated and severely delayed in delivery. The ICE-TD can have lower operational cost for this traffic, since diesel for train usage has lower tax in Denmark, and the trains fill their tanks there.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Equipment">Equipment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Equipment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ICE_decoration">ICE decoration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: ICE decoration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A notable characteristic of the ICE trains is their colour design, which has been registered by the DB as an <a href="/wiki/Geschmacksmuster" title="Geschmacksmuster">aesthetic model</a> and hence is protected as intellectual property.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The trains are painted in <i>Pale Grey</i> (<a href="/wiki/RAL_(colour_space_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="RAL (colour space system)">RAL</a> 7035) with a <i>Traffic Red</i> (RAL 3020) stripe on the lower part of the vehicle. The continuous black band of windows and their oval door windows differentiate the ICEs from any other <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">DB</a> train.</p>
<p>The ICE 1 and ICE 2 units originally had an <i>Orient Red</i> (RAL 3031) stripe, accompanied by a <i>Pastel Violet</i> stripe below (RAL 4009, 26&#160;cm wide). These stripes were repainted with the current Traffic Red between 1998 and 2000, when all ICE units were being checked and repainted in anticipation of the <a href="/wiki/EXPO_2000" class="mw-redirect" title="EXPO 2000">EXPO 2000</a>.</p>
<p>The "ICE" lettering uses the colour <i>Agate Grey</i> (RAL 7038), the frame is painted in <i>Quartz Grey</i> (RAL 7039). The plastic platings in the interior all utilise the <i>Pale Grey</i> (RAL 7035) colour tone. Originally, the ICE 1 interior was designed in pastel tones with an emphasis on mint, following the DB colour scheme of the day. The ICE 1 trains were refurbished in the mid-2000s, however, and now follow the same design as the ICE 3, which makes heavy usage of indirect lighting and wooden furnishings.</p>
<p>The distinctive ICE design was developed by a team of designers around <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Neumeister" title="Alexander Neumeister">Alexander Neumeister</a> in the early 1980s and first used on the <a href="/wiki/InterCityExperimental" title="InterCityExperimental">InterCityExperimental</a> (ICE V). The team around Neumeister then designed the ICE 1, ICE 2, and ICE 3/T/TD. The interior of the trains was designed by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jens_Peters&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jens Peters (page does not exist)">Jens Peters</a> working for BPR-Design in <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>. Among others, he was responsible for the heightened roof in the restaurant car and the special lighting. The same team also developed the design for the now discontinued <a href="/wiki/InterRegio" title="InterRegio">InterRegio</a> trains in the mid-1980s.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Differences_in_train_layouts">Differences in train layouts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Differences in train layouts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trainset_numbers">Trainset numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Trainset numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While every car in an ICE train has its own unique registration number, the trains usually remain coupled as fixed trainsets for several years. For easier reference, each has been assigned a <i>trainset number</i> that is printed over each bogie of every car. These numbers usually correspond with the registration numbers of the powerheads or cab cars.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_4653_Nederlandse_Spoorwegen_at_Brussels_Zuid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/ICE_4653_Nederlandse_Spoorwegen_at_Brussels_Zuid.jpg/220px-ICE_4653_Nederlandse_Spoorwegen_at_Brussels_Zuid.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/ICE_4653_Nederlandse_Spoorwegen_at_Brussels_Zuid.jpg/330px-ICE_4653_Nederlandse_Spoorwegen_at_Brussels_Zuid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/ICE_4653_Nederlandse_Spoorwegen_at_Brussels_Zuid.jpg/440px-ICE_4653_Nederlandse_Spoorwegen_at_Brussels_Zuid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interior_equipment">Interior equipment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Interior equipment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE2_Erste_Klasse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/ICE2_Erste_Klasse.jpg/220px-ICE2_Erste_Klasse.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/ICE2_Erste_Klasse.jpg/330px-ICE2_Erste_Klasse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/ICE2_Erste_Klasse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="300" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE2_Erste_Klasse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1st class open carriage in an ICE 2</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_2nd_class_carriage_of_ICE_3_train.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Interior_of_2nd_class_carriage_of_ICE_3_train.jpg/220px-Interior_of_2nd_class_carriage_of_ICE_3_train.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Interior_of_2nd_class_carriage_of_ICE_3_train.jpg/330px-Interior_of_2nd_class_carriage_of_ICE_3_train.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Interior_of_2nd_class_carriage_of_ICE_3_train.jpg/440px-Interior_of_2nd_class_carriage_of_ICE_3_train.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_2nd_class_carriage_of_ICE_3_train.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Interior of 2nd class carriage of ICE 3 train</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The ICE trains adhere to a high standard of technology: all cars are fully air-conditioned and nearly every seat features a <a href="/wiki/Headphone" class="mw-redirect" title="Headphone">headphone</a> jack which enables the passenger to listen to several on-board music and voice programmes as well as several radio stations. Some seats in the 1st class section (in some trains also in 2nd class) are equipped with video displays showing movies and pre-recorded infotainment programmes. Each train is equipped with special cars that feature in-train repeaters for improved <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phone</a> reception as well as designated quiet zones where the use of mobile phones is discouraged. The newer ICE 3 trains also have larger digital displays in all coaches, displaying, among other things, Deutsche Bahn advertising, the predicted arrival time at the next destination and the current speed of the train.</p>
<p>The ICE 1 was originally equipped with a passenger information system based on <a href="/wiki/Bildschirmtext" title="Bildschirmtext">BTX</a>, however this system was eventually taped over and removed in the later refurbishment. The ICE 3 trains feature <a href="/wiki/Touch_screen" class="mw-redirect" title="Touch screen">touch screen</a> terminals in some carriages, enabling travellers to print train timetables. The system is also located in the restaurant car of the ICE 2.</p>
<p>The ICE 1 fleet saw a major overhaul between 2005 and 2008, supposed to extend the lifetime of the trains by another 15 to 20 years. Seats and the interior design were adapted to the ICE 3 design, electric sockets were added to every seat, the audio and video entertainment systems were removed and electronic seat reservation indicators were added above the seats. The ICE 2 trains have been undergoing the same procedure since 2010.</p>
<p>ICE 2 trains feature electric sockets at selected seats, ICE 3 and ICE T trains have sockets at nearly every seat.</p>
<p>The ICE 3 and ICE T are similar in their interior design, but the other ICE types differ in their original design. The ICE 1, the ICE 2 and seven-car ICE T (Class 411) are equipped with a full restaurant car. The five-car ICE T (Class 415) and ICE 3 however, have been designed without a restaurant, they feature a bistro coach instead. Since 1 October 2006, smoking is prohibited in the bistro coaches, similar to the restaurant cars, which have always been non-smoking.</p>
<p>All trains feature a disabled toilet and wheelchair spaces. The ICE 1 and ICE 2 have a special conference compartment whilst the ICE 3 features a compartment suitable for small children. The ICE 3 and ICE T omit the usual train manager's compartment and have an open counter named "ServicePoint" instead.</p>
<p>An electronic display above each seat indicates the locations between which the seat has been reserved. Passengers without reservations are permitted to take seats with a blank display or seats with no reservation on the current section.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maintenance">Maintenance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Maintenance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The maintenance schedule of the trains is divided into seven steps:</p>
<ol>
<li>Every 4,000 kilometres, an inspection taking about 1½ hours is undertaken. The waste collection tanks are emptied and fresh water tanks are refilled. Acute defects (e.g. malfunctioning doors) are rectified. Furthermore, safety tests are conducted. These include checking the <a href="/wiki/Pantograph_(rail)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pantograph (rail)">pantograph</a> pressure, cleaning and checking for fissures in the rooftop insulators, inspecting transformers and checking the pantograph's current collector for wear. The wheels are also checked in this inspection.</li>
<li>Every 20,000 kilometres, a 2½ hour inspection is conducted, called <i>Nachschau</i>. In this inspection, the brakes, the <a href="/wiki/Linienzugbeeinflussung" title="Linienzugbeeinflussung">Linienzugbeeinflussung</a> systems and the anti-lock brakes are checked as well.</li>
<li>After 80,000 kilometres, the train undergoes the <i>Inspektionsstufe 1</i>. During the two modules, each lasting eight hours, the brakes receive a thorough check, as well as the air conditioning and the kitchen equipment. The batteries are checked, as well as the seats and the passenger information system.</li>
<li>Once the train has reached 240,000 kilometres, the <i>Inspektionsstufe 2</i> mandates a check of the <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motors</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bearing_(mechanical)" title="Bearing (mechanical)">bearings</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Driveshaft" class="mw-redirect" title="Driveshaft">driveshafts</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bogie" title="Bogie">bogies</a> and the couplers. This inspection is usually carried out in two modules taking eight hours each.</li>
<li>About once a year (when reaching 480,000&#160;km), the <i>Inspektionsstufe 3</i> takes place, at three times eight hours each. In addition to the other checkup phases, it includes checks on the <a href="/wiki/Pneumatics" title="Pneumatics">pneumatics</a> systems, and the transformer cooling. Maintenance work is performed inside the passenger compartment.</li>
<li>The <i>1st Revision</i> is carried out after 1.2 million km. It includes a thorough check of all components of the train and is carried out in two five-day segments.</li>
<li>The seventh and final step is the <i>2nd Revision</i>, which happens when reaching 2.4 million kilometres. The <a href="/wiki/Bogie" title="Bogie">bogies</a> are exchanged for new ones and many components of the train are disassembled and checked. This step also takes two five-day segments.</li>
</ol>
<p>Maintenance on the ICE trains is carried out in special ICE workshops located in Basel, Berlin, Cologne, Dortmund, Frankfurt, Hamburg, Leipzig<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and Munich. The train is worked upon at up to four levels at a time and fault reports are sent to the workshops in advance by the on-board computer system to keep maintenance time at a minimum.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Route_planning_and_network_layout">Route planning and network layout</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Route planning and network layout">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_TrainTrack.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ICE_TrainTrack.JPG/220px-ICE_TrainTrack.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ICE_TrainTrack.JPG/330px-ICE_TrainTrack.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ICE_TrainTrack.JPG/440px-ICE_TrainTrack.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2888" data-file-height="2160" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_TrainTrack.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ICE track close up</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_Network.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/ICE_Network.png/220px-ICE_Network.png" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/ICE_Network.png/330px-ICE_Network.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/ICE_Network.png/440px-ICE_Network.png 2x" data-file-width="1136" data-file-height="1514" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_Network.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ICE network
<div>
<ul>
<li><b>red:</b> High-speed lines for 300&#160;km/h (186&#160;mph)</li>
<li><b>orange:</b> High-speed lines for 250 to 280 &#160;km/h (156 to 175&#160;mph)</li>
<li><b>blue:</b> Upgraded lines, 200 to 230&#160;km/h (125 to 145&#160;mph)</li>
<li><b>grey:</b> Other lines, max. 160&#160;km/h (100&#160;mph)</li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICEtracks.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/ICEtracks.svg/220px-ICEtracks.svg.png" width="220" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/ICEtracks.svg/330px-ICEtracks.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/ICEtracks.svg/440px-ICEtracks.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="554" data-file-height="751" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICEtracks.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Similar to the above map, also showing frequencies.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The ICE system is a polycentric network. Connections are offered in either 30-minute, hourly or bi-hourly intervals. Furthermore, additional services run during peak times, and some services call at lesser stations during off-peak times.</p>
<p>Unlike the French <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a> or the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Shinkansen" title="Shinkansen">Shinkansen</a> systems, the vehicles, tracks and operations were not designed as an integrated whole; rather, the ICE system has been integrated into Germany's pre-existing system of railway lines instead. One of the effects of this is that the ICE 3 trains can reach a speed of 300&#160;km/h (186&#160;mph) only on some stretches of line and cannot currently reach their maximum allowed speed of 330&#160;km/h on German railway lines (though a speed of 320&#160;km/h is reached by ICE 3 in France).</p>
<p>The line most heavily utilised by ICE trains is the <a href="/wiki/Mannheim%E2%80%93Frankfurt_railway" title="Mannheim–Frankfurt railway">Mannheim–Frankfurt railway</a> between <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a> due to the bundling of many ICE lines in that region. When considering all traffic (freight, local and long distance passenger), the busiest line carrying ICE traffic is the <a href="/wiki/Munich%E2%80%93Augsburg_railway" title="Munich–Augsburg railway">Munich–Augsburg line</a>, carrying about 300 trains per day.</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Intercity-Express_lines" title="List of Intercity-Express lines">List of Intercity-Express lines</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North-South_connections">North-South connections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: North-South connections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The network's main backbone consists of six north-south lines:</p>
<ol>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Altona" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg-Altona">Hamburg-Altona</a> via <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg Hbf">Hamburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Hannover_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hannover Hbf">Hannover Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Kassel-Wilhelmsh%C3%B6he_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe railway station">Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe</a> – <a href="/wiki/Fulda_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulda railway station">Fulda Bf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Hbf">Frankfurt Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Mannheim Hbf">Mannheim Hbf</a> either via <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Karlsruhe Hbf">Karlsruhe Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Freiburg_Hauptbahnhof" title="Freiburg Hauptbahnhof">Freiburg Bf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Basel_SBB" class="mw-redirect" title="Basel SBB">Basel SBB</a> (ICE line <b>20</b>) or straight to <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Stuttgart Hbf">Stuttgart Hbf</a> (ICE line <b>22</b>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Altona" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg-Altona">Hamburg-Altona</a> – <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg Hbf">Hamburg Hbf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bremen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Bremen Hbf">Bremen Hbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Hannover_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hannover Hbf">Hannover Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Kassel-Wilhelmsh%C3%B6he_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe railway station">Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe</a> – <a href="/wiki/Fulda_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulda railway station">Fulda Bf</a> – <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Würzburg Hbf">Würzburg Hbf</a> either via <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrnberg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Nürnberg Hbf">Nürnberg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Ingolstadt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Ingolstadt Hbf">Ingolstadt Hbf</a> or <a href="/wiki/Donauw%C3%B6rth" title="Donauwörth">Donauwörth Bf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Augsburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Augsburg Hbf">Augsburg Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="München Hbf">München Hbf</a> (ICE line <b>25</b>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Altona" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg-Altona">Hamburg-Altona</a> via <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg Hbf">Hamburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Berlin-Spandau_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin-Spandau railway station">Berlin-Spandau</a> – <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Hbf">Berlin Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Berlin_S%C3%BCdkreuz_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Südkreuz railway station">Berlin Südkreuz</a> – <a href="/wiki/Leipzig_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Leipzig Hbf">Leipzig Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrnberg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Nürnberg Hbf">Nürnberg Hbf</a> either via <a href="/wiki/Augsburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Augsburg Hbf">Augsburg Hbf</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ingolstadt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Ingolstadt Hbf">Ingolstadt Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="München Hbf">München Hbf</a> (ICE line <b>28</b>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Ostbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Ostbf">Berlin Ostbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Hbf">Berlin Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Berlin-Spandau_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin-Spandau railway station">Berlin-Spandau</a> – <a href="/wiki/Braunschweig_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Braunschweig Hbf">Braunschweig Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Kassel-Wilhelmsh%C3%B6he_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe railway station">Kassel-Wilhelmshöhe</a> – <a href="/wiki/Fulda_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulda railway station">Fulda Bf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Hbf">Frankfurt Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Mannheim Hbf">Mannheim Hbf</a> either via <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Karlsruhe Hbf">Karlsruhe Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Freiburg_Hauptbahnhof" title="Freiburg Hauptbahnhof">Freiburg Bf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Basel_SBB" class="mw-redirect" title="Basel SBB">Basel SBB</a> (ICE line <b>12</b>) or via <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Stuttgart Hbf">Stuttgart Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Ulm_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulm Hbf">Ulm Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Augsburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Augsburg Hbf">Augsburg Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="München Hbf">München Hbf</a> (ICE line <b>11</b>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Centraal">Amsterdam Centraal</a> or <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Dortmund Hbf">Dortmund Hbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Duisburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Duisburg Hbf">Duisburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf Hbf">Düsseldorf Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ln_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Köln Hbf">Köln Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Main)_Flughafen_Fernbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt (Main) Flughafen Fernbahnhof">Frankfurt Flughafen</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Mannheim Hbf">Mannheim Hbf</a> either via <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Karlsruhe Hbf">Karlsruhe Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Freiburg_Hauptbahnhof" title="Freiburg Hauptbahnhof">Freiburg Bf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Basel_SBB" class="mw-redirect" title="Basel SBB">Basel SBB</a> (ICE line <b>43</b>) or via <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Stuttgart Hbf">Stuttgart Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Ulm_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulm Hbf">Ulm Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Augsburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Augsburg Hbf">Augsburg Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="München Hbf">München Hbf</a> (ICE line <b>42</b>)</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East-West_connections">East-West connections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: East-West connections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Furthermore, the network has four main East-West thoroughfares:</p>
<ol>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Berlin-Gesundbrunnen_station" title="Berlin-Gesundbrunnen station">Berlin Gesundbrunnen</a> via <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Hbf">Berlin Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Berlin_S%C3%BCdkreuz" title="Berlin Südkreuz">Berlin Südkreuz</a> – <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg Hbf">Hamburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Dammtor_station" title="Hamburg Dammtor station">Hamburg Dammtor</a> – <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Altona_station" title="Hamburg-Altona station">Hamburg Altona</a> (ICE line <b>6</b>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Ostbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Ostbf">Berlin Ostbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Hbf">Berlin Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Hannover_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hannover Hbf">Hannover Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Bielefeld_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Bielefeld Hbf">Bielefeld Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Hamm_(Westfalen)_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamm (Westfalen) railway station">Hamm (Westfalen)</a> either via <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Dortmund Hbf">Dortmund Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Essen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Essen Hbf">Essen Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Duisburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Duisburg Hbf">Duisburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf Hbf">Düsseldorf Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ln/Bonn_Flughafen_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Köln/Bonn Flughafen railway station">Köln/Bonn Flughafen</a> or via <a href="/wiki/Hagen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hagen Hbf">Hagen Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Wuppertal_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Wuppertal Hbf">Wuppertal Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Solingen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Solingen Hbf">Solingen Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ln_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Köln Hbf">Köln Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bonn_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Bonn Hbf">Bonn Hbf</a> (ICE line <b>10</b>, train partitions in Hamm)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Dresden Hbf">Dresden Hbf</a> (with some trains from <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Gesundbrunnen_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Gesundbrunnen railway station">Berlin Gesundbrunnen</a>) via <a href="/wiki/Leipzig_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Leipzig Hbf">Leipzig Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Erfurt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Erfurt Hbf">Erfurt Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Fulda_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulda railway station">Fulda Bf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Hbf">Frankfurt Hbf</a> either via <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Main)_Flughafen_Fernbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt (Main) Flughafen Fernbahnhof">Frankfurt Flughafen</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mainz_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainz Hbf">Mainz Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Wiesbaden Hbf">Wiesbaden Hbf</a> or (off-peak services) via <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Darmstadt Hbf">Darmstadt Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Mannheim Hbf">Mannheim Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Kaiserslautern_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaiserslautern Hbf">Kaiserslautern Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Saarbr%C3%BCcken_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Saarbrücken Hbf">Saarbrücken Hbf</a> (ICE line <b>50</b>, train partitions in Frankfurt Hbf)</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bottlenecks">Bottlenecks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Bottlenecks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several lines on the ICE network are highly trafficked<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, among them:</p>
<ol>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Dortmund Hbf">Dortmund Hbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Bochum_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Bochum Hbf">Bochum Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Essen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Essen Hbf">Essen Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Duisburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Duisburg Hbf">Duisburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf Hbf">Düsseldorf Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ln_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Köln Hbf">Köln Hbf</a> (<a href="/wiki/Witten/Dortmund%E2%80%93Oberhausen/Duisburg_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Witten/Dortmund–Oberhausen/Duisburg Railway">Dortmund–Duisburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cologne%E2%80%93Duisburg_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Cologne–Duisburg Railway">Cologne–Duisburg</a> lines)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Hbf">Frankfurt Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Fulda_station" title="Fulda station">Fulda</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kinzig_Valley_Railway_(Hesse)" title="Kinzig Valley Railway (Hesse)">Kinzig Valley Railway</a>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Hbf">Frankfurt Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Mannheim Hbf">Mannheim Hbf</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mannheim%E2%80%93Frankfurt_railway" title="Mannheim–Frankfurt railway">Mannheim–Frankfurt railway</a>, highest IC/ICE frequency in Germany)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Karlsruhe Hbf">Karlsruhe Hbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Freiburg_Hauptbahnhof" title="Freiburg Hauptbahnhof">Freiburg</a> to <a href="/wiki/Basel_SBB" class="mw-redirect" title="Basel SBB">Basel SBB</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rhine_Valley_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhine Valley Railway">Rhine Valley Railway</a>)</li>
</ol>
<p>(Also applies to trains in the opposite directions)</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ICE-Sprinter">ICE-Sprinter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: ICE-Sprinter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(December 2015)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The so-called "ICE-Sprinter" trains are trains with fewer stops between Germany's major cities running in the morning and evening hours. They are tailored for business travellers or long-distance commuters and are marketed by DB as an alternative to domestic flights. Some of the Sprinter services continue as normal ICE services after reaching their destination. Sprinter trains usually depart around 06:00 for morning services and 18:00 for evening services. Typically the service takes 3 hours 30 minutes, which is usually half an hour faster than a standard ICE between the same cities.</p>
<p>A reservation was mandatory on the ICE-Sprinter until December 2015. In addition to the usual 1st class service (on-seat service, free newspapers like <a href="/wiki/Financial_Times_Deutschland" title="Financial Times Deutschland">Financial Times Deutschland</a> or <a href="/wiki/Handelsblatt" title="Handelsblatt">Handelsblatt</a>), the 1st class in the Sprinter trains also offers free drinks, an on-seat breakfast or dinner and additional newspapers. In the 2nd class, newspapers are provided in the carriages at no extra cost.</p>
<p>The first Sprinter service was established between <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> in 1992. <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>-<a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> followed in 1993 and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>-Hamburg in 1994. This service ran as a <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_(train)" title="Metropolitan (train)">Metropolitan</a> service between December 1996 and December 2004. In 1998, a Berlin-Frankfurt service was introduced and a service between Cologne and <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a> ran between December 2005 and October 2006.</p>
<p>Until December 2006, a morning Sprinter service ran between Frankfurt and Munich (with an intermediate stop at <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a>), taking 3:25 hours for the journey. This has been since replaced by a normal ICE connection taking only 3:21 hours.</p>
<p>Starting with the December 2017 schedule change, a new Sprinter line will link <a href="/wiki/Berlin_main_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin main station">Berlin main station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Munich_main_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Munich main station">Munich main station</a> in less than four hours.</p>
<p>As of January 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the individual ICE Sprinter lines are:</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>

<th>Departure station</th>
<th>Intermediate stops</th>
<th>Destination</th>
<th>Travel time (hh:mm)</th>
<th>Time of day</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1091<br />
1093</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Berlin_Ostbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Ostbf">Berlin Ostbf</a></td>
