<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Line_segments_abroad">Line segments abroad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Line segments abroad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_train_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/ICE_train_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station.jpg/220px-ICE_train_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/ICE_train_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station.jpg/330px-ICE_train_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/ICE_train_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station.jpg/440px-ICE_train_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_train_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ICE train at Amsterdam Central station</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif/350px-Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif" width="350" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif/525px-Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif/700px-Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif 2x" data-file-width="1980" data-file-height="1316" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The ICE network is an integral part of Europe's high speed rail system.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_Network_Austria.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/ICE_Network_Austria.svg/350px-ICE_Network_Austria.svg.png" width="350" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/ICE_Network_Austria.svg/525px-ICE_Network_Austria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/ICE_Network_Austria.svg/700px-ICE_Network_Austria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1997" data-file-height="1050" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_Network_Austria.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lines to and in Austria</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Some ICE trains also run on services abroad – sometimes diverting from their original lines.</p>
<ol>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Duisburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Duisburg Hbf">Duisburg Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Centraal">Amsterdam Centraal</a> (<a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ln_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Köln Hbf">Köln Hbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Aachen Hbf">Aachen Hbf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge-Guillemins" class="mw-redirect" title="Liège-Guillemins">Liège-Guillemins</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bruxelles-Midi_/_Brussel-Zuid_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Bruxelles-Midi / Brussel-Zuid railway station">Bruxelles-Midi/Brussel-Zuid</a> (<a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Saarbr%C3%BCcken_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Saarbrücken Hbf">Saarbrücken Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_l%27Est" class="mw-redirect" title="Gare de l'Est">Paris Est</a> (<a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Basel_SBB" class="mw-redirect" title="Basel SBB">Basel SBB</a> to <a href="/wiki/Interlaken_Ost_railway_station" title="Interlaken Ost railway station">Interlaken Ost</a> (<a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Basel_SBB" class="mw-redirect" title="Basel SBB">Basel SBB</a> to <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich_HB" class="mw-redirect" title="Zürich HB">Zürich HB</a> (<a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Stuttgart Hbf">Stuttgart Hbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Schaffhausen" title="Schaffhausen">Schaffhausen</a> to <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich_HB" class="mw-redirect" title="Zürich HB">Zürich HB</a> (<a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>) (Now branded as <a href="/wiki/Intercity_(Deutsche_Bahn)" title="Intercity (Deutsche Bahn)">IC</a> service)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="München Hbf">München Hbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Kufstein" title="Kufstein">Kufstein</a> to <a href="/wiki/Innsbruck_Hauptbahnhof" title="Innsbruck Hauptbahnhof">Innsbruck Hbf</a> (<a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="München Hbf">München Hbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Salzburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Salzburg Hbf">Salzburg Hbf</a> – <a href="/wiki/Linz_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Linz Hbf">Linz Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wien_Westbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Wien Westbahnhof">Wien Westbf</a> (<a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Passau_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Passau Hbf">Passau Hbf</a> via <a href="/wiki/Linz_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Linz Hbf">Linz Hbf</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wien_Westbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Wien Westbahnhof">Wien Westbf</a> (<a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Flensburg_station" title="Flensburg station">Flensburg</a> to <a href="/wiki/Aarhus_Central_Station" title="Aarhus Central Station">Aarhus Central</a> (<a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>)</li>
<li>from <a href="/wiki/Puttgarden_station" title="Puttgarden station">Puttgarden</a> to <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Central_Station" title="Copenhagen Central Station">København H</a> (<a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>)</li>
</ol>
<p>(Also applies to the opposite directions)</p>
<p>Since December 2006, <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Stuttgart Hbf">Stuttgart Hbf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich_HB" class="mw-redirect" title="Zürich HB">Zürich HB</a> have been connected by a bi-hourly service. This service however has been replaced by a daily <a href="/wiki/Intercity_(Deutsche_Bahn)" title="Intercity (Deutsche Bahn)">Intercity</a> service since March 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/%C3%96sterreichische_Bundesbahnen" class="mw-redirect" title="Österreichische Bundesbahnen">ÖBB</a> in Austria also uses two ICE T trainsets (classified as <a href="/wiki/%C3%96BB_Class_4011" title="ÖBB Class 4011">ÖBB Class 4011</a>) between <a href="/wiki/Wien_Westbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Wien Westbahnhof">Wien Westbahnhof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Innsbruck_Hauptbahnhof" title="Innsbruck Hauptbahnhof">Innsbruck Hauptbahnhof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bregenz" title="Bregenz">Bregenz</a> (without stops in Germany), although they do not use tilting technology. Since December 2007 ÖBB and DB offer a bi-hourly connection between <a href="/wiki/Wien_Westbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Wien Westbahnhof">Wien Westbf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hauptbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Hauptbahnhof">Frankfurt Hbf</a>.</p>
<p>Since June 2007 ICE 3M trains have been running between <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Hbf">Frankfurt Hbf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_l%27Est" class="mw-redirect" title="Gare de l'Est">Paris Est</a> via <a href="/wiki/Saarbr%C3%BCcken" title="Saarbrücken">Saarbrücken</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kaiserslautern" title="Kaiserslautern">Kaiserslautern</a>. Together with the <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a>-operated service between <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_l%27Est" class="mw-redirect" title="Gare de l'Est">Paris Est</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Stuttgart Hbf">Stuttgart Hbf</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="München Hbf">München Hbf</a>, this ICE line is part of the "<a href="/wiki/LGV_Est" title="LGV Est">LGV Est européenne</a>", also called "Paris-Ostfrankreich-Süddeutschland" (or <a href="/wiki/SNCF_TGV_POS" title="SNCF TGV POS">POS</a>) for short, a pan-European high-speed line between France and Germany.</p>
<p>Since late 2007, ICE TD trains have linked <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Hbf">Berlin Hbf</a> with <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aarhus" title="Aarhus">Aarhus</a> via <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg Hbf">Hamburg Hbf</a>.</p>
<p>In addition, ICE Trains to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a> are on the horizon, perhaps in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-bahn.com_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bahn.com-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-london_delay_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-london_delay-5">[5]</a></sup> Unique safety and security requirements for the tunnel (such as airport-style checks at stations) as well as hold-ups in the production of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Velaro-D&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Velaro-D (page does not exist)">Velaro-D</a> trains to be used on the route<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> have delayed these plans.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intra-Swiss_ICE_trains">Intra-Swiss ICE trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Intra-Swiss ICE trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To avoid empty runs or excess waits, several services exist that operate exclusively inside Switzerland:</p>
<ul>
<li>three services from <a href="/wiki/Basel_SBB" class="mw-redirect" title="Basel SBB">Basel SBB</a> to <a href="/wiki/Interlaken_Ost_railway_station" title="Interlaken Ost railway station">Interlaken Ost</a></li>
<li>two services from <a href="/wiki/Basel_SBB" class="mw-redirect" title="Basel SBB">Basel SBB</a> to <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich_HB" class="mw-redirect" title="Zürich HB">Zürich HB</a></li>
<li>three service from <a href="/wiki/Interlaken_Ost_railway_station" title="Interlaken Ost railway station">Interlaken Ost</a> to <a href="/wiki/Basel_SBB" class="mw-redirect" title="Basel SBB">Basel SBB</a></li>
<li>one service from <a href="/wiki/Interlaken_Ost_railway_station" title="Interlaken Ost railway station">Interlaken Ost</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bern_railway_station" title="Bern railway station">Bern</a></li>
<li>two services from <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich_HB" class="mw-redirect" title="Zürich HB">Zürich HB</a> to <a href="/wiki/Basel_SBB" class="mw-redirect" title="Basel SBB">Basel SBB</a></li>
<li>one service from <a href="/wiki/Bern_railway_station" title="Bern railway station">Bern</a> to <a href="/wiki/Interlaken_Ost_railway_station" title="Interlaken Ost railway station">Interlaken Ost</a></li>
</ul>
<p>These trains, despite being officially notated as ICEs, are more comparable to a Swiss <a href="/wiki/InterRegio" title="InterRegio">InterRegio</a> or <a href="/wiki/RegioExpress" title="RegioExpress">RegioExpress</a> train, calling at small stations like <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6hlin" title="Möhlin">Möhlin</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sissach" title="Sissach">Sissach</a>. As common in Switzerland, these trains can be used without paying extra for a supplement.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents">Accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There have been several accidents involving ICE trains. The Eschede disaster was the only accident with fatalities inside the train, but other accidents have resulted in major damage to the trainsets involved.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eschede_disaster">Eschede disaster</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Eschede disaster">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eschede_train_disaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Eschede train disaster">Eschede train disaster</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ice_eschede_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Ice_eschede_1.jpg/220px-Ice_eschede_1.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Ice_eschede_1.jpg/330px-Ice_eschede_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Ice_eschede_1.jpg/440px-Ice_eschede_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="385" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ice_eschede_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Eschede site – Remains of ICE&#160;884 "Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The ICE accident near <a href="/wiki/Eschede" title="Eschede">Eschede</a> that happened on 3 June 1998 was a severe <a href="/wiki/Lists_of_rail_accidents" title="Lists of rail accidents">railway accident</a>. Trainset 51, travelling as <b>ICE 884</b> "<a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Conrad_R%C3%B6ntgen" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen">Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen</a>" from Munich to Hamburg, derailed at 200&#160;km/h (125&#160;mph), killing 101 and injuring 88. It remains the world's worst high-speed rail disaster.</p>
<p>The cause of the accident was a wheel rim which broke and damaged the train six kilometres south of the accident site. The wheel rim penetrated the carriage floor and lifted the check rail of a set of <a href="/wiki/Railroad_switch" title="Railroad switch">points</a> close to Eschede station. The broken-off check rail then forced the point blades of the following set of points to change direction, and the rear cars of the trainset were diverted to a different track. They hit the pillars of a street overpass, which then collapsed onto the tracks. Only three cars and the front powerhead passed under the bridge, the rest of the 14-car train jackknifed into the collapsed bridge.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_accidents">Other accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Other accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:4011592_Unfall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/4011592_Unfall.jpg/150px-4011592_Unfall.jpg" width="150" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/4011592_Unfall.jpg/225px-4011592_Unfall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/4011592_Unfall.jpg/300px-4011592_Unfall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="667" data-file-height="1000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:4011592_Unfall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damaged <i>ICE T</i> trainset 1192</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 27 September 2001, trainset 5509 fell off a work platform at the <a href="/wiki/Hof,_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Hof, Germany">Hof</a> maintenance facility and was written off.</p>
<p>On 22 November 2001, powerhead <i>401 020</i> caught fire. The train was stopped at the station in <a href="/wiki/Offenbach_am_Main" title="Offenbach am Main">Offenbach am Main</a> near Frankfurt a.M. No passengers were harmed, but the fire caused the powerhead to be written off.</p>
<p>On 6 January 2004, ICE TD trainset 1106 caught fire while it was parked at <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a>. Two cars were written off, and the others are now used as spares.</p>
<p>On 1 April 2004, trainset 321 collided with a <a href="/wiki/Tractor" title="Tractor">tractor</a> that had fallen onto the track at a tunnel entrance near <a href="/wiki/Efringen-Kirchen" title="Efringen-Kirchen">Istein</a>, and was derailed. No-one was injured. Trainset 321 was temporarily taken apart, its cars being switched with cars from other ICE 3 trainsets.</p>
<p>Powerhead <i>401 553</i> suffered major damage in a collision with a car on the <a href="/wiki/Mannheim%E2%80%93Frankfurt_railway" title="Mannheim–Frankfurt railway">Mannheim–Frankfurt railway</a> in April 2006.</p>
<p>On 28 April 2006, trainset 73 collided head-on with two <a href="/wiki/SBB-CFF-FFS_Re_460" title="SBB-CFF-FFS Re 460">BLS Re 465</a> locomotives at <a href="/wiki/Thun" title="Thun">Thun</a> in Switzerland. The driver of the Swiss locomotives was unfamiliar with the new layout of the station, which had been recently changed. He did not see a shunting signal ordering him to stop. The locomotives automatically engaged the emergency brakes when he passed the signal, but came to a stop on the same track as the approaching ICE. The ICE was travelling at a speed of 74&#160;km/h. The emergency brake slowed the train to 56&#160;km/h at the point of collision. 30 passengers and the driver of the ICE suffered minor injuries, the driver of the Swiss locomotives having jumped to safety. Both trains suffered major damage. The powerhead <i>401 573</i> had to be rebuilt using components from three damaged powerheads (<i>401 573</i>, <i>401 020</i> and <i>401 551</i>).</p>
<p>On 1 March 2008, trainset 1192, travelling as ICE 23, collided with a tree which had fallen onto the track near <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BChl,_North_Rhine-Westphalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Brühl, North Rhine-Westphalia">Brühl</a> after being blown down by <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Emma_(2008)" title="Cyclone Emma (2008)">Cyclone Emma</a>. The driver suffered severe injuries. The trainset is back in service, its driving-car having been replaced with that from trainset 1106.</p>
<p>On 26 April 2008, trainset 11, travelling as ICE 885, collided with a herd of sheep on the <a href="/wiki/Hanover-W%C3%BCrzburg_high-speed_rail_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanover-Würzburg high-speed rail line">Hanover-Würzburg high-speed rail line</a> near <a href="/wiki/Fulda" title="Fulda">Fulda</a>. Both powerheads and ten of the 12 cars derailed. The train came to a stop 1300 metres into the <a href="/wiki/Landr%C3%BCckentunnel" class="mw-redirect" title="Landrückentunnel">Landrückentunnel</a>. 19 of the 130 passengers suffered mostly minor injuries, four of them needing hospital treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>A cracked axle was blamed for a low-speed derailment of a third-generation ICE in Cologne in July 2008. The accident, in which no-one was hurt, caused DB to recall its newest ICEs as a safety measure.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> In October 2008, the company recalled its ICE-T trains after a further crack was found.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 April 2010, ICE 105 Amsterdam - Basel lost a door while travelling at high speed near <a href="/wiki/Montabaur" title="Montabaur">Montabaur</a>. The door slammed into the side of ICE 612 on the adjacent track. Six people travelling on ICE 612 were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 August 2010, the ICE from Frankfurt to Paris hit a truck that had slid from an embankment on to the rail near <a href="/wiki/Lambrecht,_Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Lambrecht, Rhineland-Palatinate">Lambrecht</a>. The first two carriages derailed and ten people were injured, one seriously.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 January 2011, trainset 4654 partly derailed during a side-on collision with a freight train near <a href="/wiki/Zevenaar" title="Zevenaar">Zevenaar</a> in the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> There were no injuries.</p>
<p>On 2 May 2017, a trainset was derailed at <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Hauptbahnhof" title="Dortmund Hauptbahnhof">Dortmund Hauptbahnhof</a>. Two people were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-Local020517_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Local020517-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fare_structure">Fare structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Fare structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>ICE trains are the highest category (Class A) trains in the fare system of the Deutsche Bahn. Their fares are not calculated on a fixed per-kilometre table as with other trains, but instead have fixed prices for station-to-station connections, depending on a multitude of factors including the railway line category and the general demand on the line. Even on lines where the ICE is not faster than an ordinary <a href="/wiki/Intercity_(Deutsche_Bahn)" title="Intercity (Deutsche Bahn)">IC</a> or <a href="/wiki/EuroCity" title="EuroCity">EC</a> train (for example Hamburg to Dortmund), an additional surcharge will be levied on the ground that the ICE trains have a higher comfort level than IC/EC trains.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the Netherlands, a comparably low €2,40 surcharge has to be paid for each trip on the "ICE International" when travellers are not holding an international ticket. Only passengers with a student travel card or a NS-Business card can travel within the Netherlands without having to pay the surcharge.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Austria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On the intra-Austrian lines (Vienna-Innsbruck-Bregenz, Vienna-Salzburg(-Munich), Vienna-Passau(-Hamburg) and Innsbruck-Kufstein(-Berlin)) no additional fees are charged.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Likewise, the trains running to and from <a href="/wiki/Zurich" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich">Zurich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interlaken" title="Interlaken">Interlaken</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chur" title="Chur">Chur</a>, as well as those on the intra-Swiss ICE trains (see above) can be used without any surcharge.</p>
<p>In Switzerland and Austria, a ride on the ICE takes nearly as long as on a domestic train. This is because of the comparably short length of travel and the low speeds in these countries (often no more than 160&#160;km/h, sometimes 200&#160;km/h) when compared to Germany.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The ICE trains Hamburg – Copenhagen cost the same as the EuroCity trains, there being no other trains. The ICE trains Hamburg – Aarhus have a surcharge of €9 as against other trains (for which two changes are needed). Inside Denmark the ICE trains have the same fare as regional trains.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scale_models">Scale models</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Scale models">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Various ICE train scale models in several scales have been produced by <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A4rklin" title="Märklin">Märklin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fleischmann_(model_railroads)" title="Fleischmann (model railroads)">Fleischmann</a><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary.2C_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (October 2013)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, <a href="/wiki/Roco" title="Roco">Roco</a><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary.2C_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (October 2013)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, <a href="/wiki/Trix_(company)" title="Trix (company)">Trix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mehano" title="Mehano">Mehano</a>, <a href="/wiki/PIKO" title="PIKO">PIKO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary.2C_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (October 2013)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and Lima<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary.2C_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (October 2013)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_future_services">Possible future services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Possible future services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="London">London</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: London">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2010, the European railway network was opened to a liberalisation intended to allow greater competition.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Both <a href="/wiki/Air_France-KLM" class="mw-redirect" title="Air France-KLM">Air France-KLM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> have indicated their desire to take advantage of the new laws to run new services via the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1</a> route that terminates at London St Pancras.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ES-DB1_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ES-DB1-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_at_St_Pancras.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/ICE_at_St_Pancras.JPG/220px-ICE_at_St_Pancras.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/ICE_at_St_Pancras.JPG/330px-ICE_at_St_Pancras.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/ICE_at_St_Pancras.JPG/440px-ICE_at_St_Pancras.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE_at_St_Pancras.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ICE at St Pancras with commemorative decals</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A test run of an ICE train through the Channel Tunnel took place on 19 October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-rg-ice3-chunnel_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg-ice3-chunnel-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rn2010_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rn2010-39">[39]</a></sup> Passenger-carrying ICE trains, however, will have to meet safety requirements in order to transit the Channel Tunnel. Although the requirement for splittable trains was lifted, concerns remain over the shorter length of ICE trainsets,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[note 1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rn2010_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rn2010-39">[39]</a></sup> fire safety,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[note 2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rg-ice3-chunnel_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg-ice3-chunnel-38">[38]</a></sup> and the ICE's <a href="/wiki/Distributed_power" title="Distributed power">distributed power</a> arrangements. There have been suggestions that French interests have advocated stringent enforcement to delay a competitor on the route.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> Eurostar also recently chose <a href="/wiki/Siemens_Velaro" title="Siemens Velaro">Siemens Velaro</a>-based rolling stock; there were concerns that <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a> (builders of the passenger trains that already use the Tunnel) and the French Government would take the matter to court.<sup id="cite_ref-rn2010_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rn2010-39">[39]</a></sup> In October 2010, the French transport minister suggested that the <a href="/wiki/European_Railway_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="European Railway Agency">European Railway Agency</a> (based in France) should arbitrate.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> After safety rule changes which might permit the use of Siemens Velaro rolling stock, the French government dismissed their delegate to the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel_Safety_Authority" title="Channel Tunnel Safety Authority">Channel Tunnel Safety Authority</a>, and brought in a replacement.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2011, a European Rail Agency report authorized trains with distributed traction for use in the Channel Tunnel. This means that the ICE class 407 trains which DB intends to use for its London services will be able to run through the tunnel. In February 2014, however, Deutsche Bahn announced further difficulties with launching the route, and reports make it seem unlikely that service will start anytime this decade.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2017 it was announced that Deutsche Bahn had revived plans for a London to Frankfurt train service with the service beginning as early as 2020. The service would take around 5 hours and could rival airlines and become the first competitor for Eurostar.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Munich-Zurich">Munich-Zurich</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Munich-Zurich">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A new ICE service from <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> to <a href="/wiki/Zurich" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich">Zurich</a> via <a href="/wiki/Lindau" title="Lindau">Lindau</a> is planned to start after 2020 when the electrification and modernization works in the 150&#160;km section between <a href="/wiki/Geltendorf" title="Geltendorf">Geltendorf</a> and Lindau will be completed. The journey times will be then cut by 45min to less than 3 hours and 30 minutes and the line between Munich and Zurich is expected to be served by up to eight trains per day running at speeds up to 160&#160;km/h.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ridership">Ridership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Ridership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<tr>
<td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source: <sup id="cite_ref-whhh_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whhh-50">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-siemenspic_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siemenspic-51">[49]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>From its inception in July 1991 to 2006, ICE has transported roughly 550 million passengers, including 67 million in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> The cumulative sum of passengers is roughly 1.25 billion in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-siemenspic_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siemenspic-51">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 5 October 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Post_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Deutsche Post AG">Deutsche Post AG</a> released a series of stamps, among them a stamp picturing an ICE 3, at 55+25 euro cents.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">Lego</a> modelled one of its <a href="/wiki/Lego_train" class="mw-redirect" title="Lego train">train sets</a> after the ICE.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> A Railworks add on is available for Train Simulator 2012 accurately reflecting the original 1991 version of the ICE on German tracks (Siegen to Hagen).<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> There is also an addon utilising the Munich - Augsburg line using ICE 3 trainsets.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intercity-Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">ICE is too short to ensure sufficient proximity to tunnel emergency exits, but DB claims that a Tunnel safety exercise on 18 October 2010 had been "highly successful".</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The current Velaro ICE3MF sets would not meet the specialized fire safety requirements for the carriage of passengers through the Channel Tunnel, but the future <a href="/wiki/Siemens_Velaro" title="Siemens Velaro">Siemens Velaro</a> ICE-3D sets (due to enter service in later 2010) include the necessary additional fire-proofing.</span></li>
</ol>
